failure to do so would amount to violation of this code of integrity and all bidder must be asked in the tender document to declare any previous transgressions of such code of integrity with any entity in any country during the last three years or of being debarred by any other procuring entity
failure to do so would amount to violation of this code of integrity the must disclose any commissions or fees that may have been paid or are to be paid to agents representatives or commission agents concerning the selection process or execution and performance of the contract
the information disclosed must include the name and address of the agent representative or commission agent the amount and currency and the purpose of the commission or fee in format given in the tender document
to encourage voluntary disclosures such declarations would not mean automatic disqualification for the bidder making such declarations
the declared conflict of interest may be evaluated and mitigation steps if possible may be taken by the procuring entity
similarly voluntary reporting of previous transgressions of code of integrity elsewhere may be evaluated and barring cases of various grades of debarment an alert watch may be kept on the bidders actions in the tender and subsequent contract
conflict of interest in case of consultants professionalism the consultant is required to provide professional objective and impartial advice at all times holding the procuring entity interests paramount above own corporate interests and above any consideration for future work strictly avoiding any conflicts of interest
cipp and conflict of interest all bidders shall have to abide by the code of integrity in public procurement detailed in the tender document including conflict of interest
without limitation on the generality of the foregoing and unless stated otherwise in the rfp document the consultant shall not be hired under the circumstances set forth in following conflicting assignments consultants including its experts and consultants or its allied shall not be hired for any assignment that by its nature may be in conflict with another assignment of the consultant or its allied firm for the same or for another procuring entity
firm or its allied firms that has been engaged by the client to provide goods works or services for project or any of its affiliates shall be disqualified from providing consultancy service resulting from or directly related to those goods works or services
conversely firm or its allied firms hired to provide consultancy services for the preparation or implementation of project or any of its affiliates shall be disqualified from subsequently providing goods or works or services resulting from or directly related to the consultancy services for such preparation or implementation conflicting bidding bidder shall not have conflict of interest with other bidders
such conflict of interest can lead to practices to the detriment of procuring entity interests
all bidders found to have conflict of interest shall be for definition of allied firm please refer to procurement glossary section
bidder may be considered to have conflict of interest with one or more parties in this tender process if firm shall submit only one proposal either individually or as jv partner in another proposal
if firm including jv partner submits or participates in more than one proposal all such proposals shall be disqualified
this does not however preclude firm from participating as or an individual consultant to participate as team member in more than one proposal when circumstances justify but only if permitted by the rfp document
directly or indirectly controls is controlled by or is under common control with another bidder or iii receives or have received any direct or indirect financial stake from another bidder or iv has the same legal agent as another bidder for purposes of this bid
principal can authorize only one agent and an agent also should not represent or quote on behalf of more than one principal or vi has relationship with another bidder directly or through common third parties which puts it in position to have access to information about or influence the bid of another bidder or influence the decisions of the procuring entity regarding this tender process or vii in case of holding company having more than one independent units or more than one unit having common business only one unit should quote
similar restrictions would apply to closely related allied firms
bidders must proactively declare such common management units in similar line of business
conflicting relationships consultant including experts and consultants that has close business or family with professional staff of the procuring entity who are directly or indirectly involved in any part of the preparation of tor for the assignment ii selection process for the contract or iii supervision of the contract may not be awarded contract unless the conflict stemming from this relationship has been resolved in manner acceptable to the client throughout the selection process and execution of the contract
unfair competitive advantage in case of consultants fairness and transparency in the selection process require that the consultants or their affiliates competing for specific assignment do not derive an unfair competitive advantage from having provided consultancy services related to the assignment in question
such unfair competitive advantage is best avoided by full transparency and by providing equal opportunity so that all firms or individuals interested or involved have full information about service assignment and its nature scope and background information
to that end the request for proposals and all information would be made available to all consultants simultaneously
punitive provisions without prejudice to and in addition to the rights of the procuring entity to other penal provisions as per the bid documents or contract if the procuring entity concludes that please refer to example in para for clarification prospective service provider directly or through an agent has violated this code of integrity in competing for the contract or in executing contract the procuring entity may take appropriate measures including one or more of the following if his bids are under consideration in any procurement forfeiture or encashment of bid security calling off of any negotiations and iii rejection and exclusion of the bidder from the procurement process if contract has already been awarded cancellation of the relevant contract and recovery of compensation for loss incurred by the procuring entity forfeiture or encashment of any other security or bond relating to the procurement iii recovery of payments made by the procuring entity along with interest thereon at the prevailing rate provisions in addition to above removal from the list of registered suppliers and debarment of the bidder from participation in future procurements of the procuring entity for period for period not exceeding two years in case of practices information for further processing may be filed under signature of the joint secretary level officer with the competition commission of india iii initiation of suitable disciplinary or criminal proceedings against any individual or staff found responsible
integrity pact ip the integrity pact is tool to help governments businesses and civil society to fight corruption in public contracting
it binds both buyers and sellers to ethical conduct and transparency in all activities from of bidders bidding and contracting implementation completion and operation related to the contract
this removes insecurity of bidders that while they themselves may abjure bribery but their competitors may resort to it and win contract by unfair means
ministry of finance department of expenditure have departments and their subordinate offices including autonomous bodies to incorporate integrity pact as per format in annexure by depending on the nature of contracts above threshold value
cvc issued revised standard operating circular dtd and stated that in view of the increasing procurement activities of public sector banks psbs public sector insurance companies dated july dated july manual for procurement of consultancy services psics and financial institutions fis shall also adopt and implement the suggested format of integrity
the nature of procurement and threshold of value is to be decided by the departments with approval of the minister in charge
as guidance the threshold should be such as to cover bulk eighty to ninety percent by value of its procurement expenditure
the pact essentially envisages an agreement between the prospective and the buyer committing the of both sides not to resort to any corrupt practices in any of the contract
only those who commit themselves to such pact with the buyer would be considered competent to participate in the bidding process
in other words entering into this pact would be preliminary qualification
the essential ingredients of the pact include promise on the part of the procuring entity to treat all bidders with equity and reason and not to seek or accept any benefit which is not legally available promise on the part of bidders not to offer any benefit to the employees of the procuring entity not available legally promise on the part of bidders not to enter into any undisclosed agreement or understanding with other bidders with respect to prices specifications certifications subsidiary contracts etc promise on the part of bidders not to pass any information provided by principal as part of business relationship to others and also not to commit any offence under prevention of corruption act or indian penal code foreign bidders to disclose the name and address of agents and representatives in india and indian bidders to disclose their foreign principals or allied firms bidders to disclose the payments to be made by them to agents brokers or any other intermediary bidders to disclose any transgressions with any other government organization that may impinge on the principle
the date of such transgression for the purpose of disclosure by the bidders in this regard would be the date on which cognizance of the said transgression was taken by the competent authority
the period for which such transgression are to be reported by the bidders shall be the last three years to be reckoned from date of bid submission
the transgression for which cognizance was taken even before the specified period of three years but are pending conclusion shall also be reported by the bidders
any violation of integrity pact would entail disqualification of the bidders and exclusion from future business dealings as per the existing provisions of gfr pc act and other financial guidelines etc
as may be applicable to the organization concerned integrity pact would be implemented through panel of independent external monitors iems
all organisations are called upon to make sincere and sustained efforts to imbibe the spirit and principles of the integrity pact and ensure its effective implementation
the final responsibility for implementing integrity pact vests with the head of
the procurement wing of the organisation would be the focal point for the implementation of integrity pact
the provision for the integrity pact is to be included in all requests for documents issued in future in respect of the procurements that meet the criteria laid down in para above
in all tenders covered under the integrity pact particulars of all iems including their email ids should be mentioned instead of mentioning details of single iem
through an appropriate provision in the tender document it must be ensured that the integrity pact is deemed as part of the contract so that its conditions bind the parties concerned
clause should be included in the integrity pact that person signing the integrity pact shall not approach the courts while representing the matters to iems and they shall await their decision
in the case of joint venture all the partners of the joint venture should sign the integrity pact
in the case of the principal contractor shall take responsibility for the adoption of integrity pact by the
it is to be ensured that all contractors also sign the integrity pact
in the case of the tp shall be partite arrangement to be signed by the organization the contractor and the
in respect of particular contract the integrity pact shall be operative from the date both parties sign it
further details about appointment and role of iems is given in the to the annexure integrity pact
development of new sources and of firms normally in open tendering there should be no restriction of prior registration
entities may provide for registration after selection in unrestricted open tendering
difference may be noted between registration empanelment maintaining classified list of firms based on their experience usually required in case of limited tenders and prequalification
registration is to establish genuine identification of the firm for portals preferential procurement and so on
empanelment is to establish capability for restricted tendering not open tendering limited tendering panels also useful in special limited tenders
and lists wherever the nature of requirement dictates competition only among equally qualified bidders without vitiation of prices offered by unqualified bidders prequalification may be done with open tendering in the prequalification bidding stage
if there are frequent requirements of such nature prequalification may be done through open process with extended validity of shortlist of qualified bidders called list of approved sources in some organisations ministry of railways for example one year or longer
such use of list of qualified bidders is known as list in many countries as distinct from limited tender panel which does not undergo formal process
however since in common parlance registration is word interchangeably for the above three concepts used by most of departments this usage is being retained though the distinction would be clear from the context of usage
for goods and services not available on gem and for works head of department may register firms for requirements which are specifically used by that department or office periodically
ensuring an and current list of registered capable and competent firms facilitates efficiency economy and promotion of competition in public procurement especially while floating limited local direct contracting
for such tenders it may be possible to skip bidder qualification to avoid unnecessary duplication of efforts thereby saving time especially in the case of emergency procurement
registration of the firms should be done following fair transparent and reasonable procedure and after giving due publicity
in case of goods and services such registered firms should be on gem as and when the item or service gets listed on gem
the list of registered firms should for the subject matter of procurement be exhibited on websites of the procuring their portals
ministries departments with significant volume of procurements may follow their own policies and procedures for registration of firms if already existing
the policies and procedures for registration described below is for guidance of departments who do not have their own laid down procedures for this
the department shall announce the authorities competent to deal with the applications and grant registrations along with their jurisdictions
the appellate authority shall be at least one level above the registering authority or as designated by the department
all department may use such lists prepared by other ministries departments as and when necessary
registered firms are ordinarily exempted from furnishing earnest money bid security with their tenders for items and monetary limits for which they are registered

registration should be for specific trade groups of
for this purpose all should be divided into trade groups and the information published on the relevant websites it should be mentioned in the letter of registration that the registration is valid for fixed period one to three years
at the end of this period the registered firm willing to continue with registration are to apply afresh for renewal of registration
however the registration would be initially treated as provisional and it would be treated as confirmed only after the firm has satisfactorily executed one order of the relevant category and value from procuring entity
the extension of validity of registration is not matter of right and procuring entity reserves the right not to extend such registration without assigning any reason all registered firms should be allocated unique registration number
once the firms are registered circular shall be issued by the registration authority indicating the names and addresses of the registered firms with details of the requirements and monetary value they will supply as well as the validity period and so on for which they are registered

in other categories and higher monetary limits the firm would be treated as any unregistered firm and not be entitled to the privileges of registered firm
the monetary limit or category so laid down does not however debar firm from getting orders more than the monetary limit or for other categories provided the procuring entity is satisfied about the capacity and capability of the firm but requisite security deposit should be obtained as is being done in the case of unregistered firms performance and conduct of every registered firm are to be watched by the concerned department
procuring entity should also reserve the right to remove firms who do not perform satisfactorily even during the validity of registration after giving due opportunity to the firm to make representation if they fail to abide by the terms and conditions of the registration or fail to execute contracts on time or provide services or make any false declaration to any government agency or for any ground which in the opinion of the government is not in public interest procuring entity shall retain its option to reassess firms already registered at any later date to satisfy itself about the current financial worthiness facilities available and so on
thereafter procuring entity may decide to retain them as registered suppliers for the requirements and monetary limit earlier considered or with necessary changes as deemed fit
in case of adverse reports from the team of procuring entity officers who reassess the firm procuring entity shall delete such firm from the registered suppliers list rule of gfr
rule of general financial rules gfr registration of suppliers and their eligibility to participate in procurement entity procurements is subject to compliance with code of integrity for public procurement and satisfactory performance in contracts
rule of general financial rules gfr states the following regarding the debarment from bidding bidder shall be debarred if he has been convicted of an under the prevention of corruption act or the indian penal code or any other law for the time being in force for causing any loss of life or property or causing threat to public health as part of execution of public procurement contract
bidder debarred under or any successor of the bidder shall not be eligible to participate in procurement process of any procuring entity for period not exceeding three years commencing from the date of debarment
the procuring entity may debar bidder or any of its successors from participating in any procurement process undertaken by it for period not exceeding two years if it determines that the bidder has breached the code of integrity
the bidder shall not be debarred unless such bidder has been given reasonable opportunity to represent against such debarment
current guidelines on debarment of firms from bidding ppd doe did consultations on the issue of debarment with major procuring departments and issued the following debarment guidelines in suppression to all earlier instructions on this
the guidelines are classified under following two types in cases where debarment is proposed to be limited to single ministry the appropriate orders can be issued by that ministry itself thereby banning all its business dealing with the debarred firm
where it is proposed to extend the debarment beyond the jurisdiction of the ministry covering to all central departments the requisite orders shall be issued by department of expenditure doe ministry of finance mof
firm the term or has the same meaning for the purpose of these guidelines which includes an individual or person company cooperative society hindu undivided family and an association or body of persons whether incorporated or not engaged in trade or business
allied firm all concerns which come within the sphere of effective influence of the debarred firms shall be treated as allied firms
in determining this the following vide om no
issued by department of expenditure dated factors may be taken into consideration please also refer to procurement glossary section whether the management is common majority interest in the management is held by the partners or directors of suspended firm iii substantial or majority shares are owned by the suspended firm and by virtue of this it has controlling voice
iv directly or indirectly controls or is controlled by or is under common control with another bidder
all successor firms will also be considered as allied firms
the terms banning of firm suspension etc
convey the same meaning as of debarment
debarment by single department orders for debarment of firm shall be passed by keeping in view of the following grounds for debarment bidder including its allied firms may be debarred from participating in any procurement process for period not exceeding two years along with such other actions as may be permissible under law for following reasons if it is determined that the bidder has breached the code of integrity as per rule of gfrs
refer to para of this manual for code of integrity
false declaration of local content by class class ii local suppliers under public procurement preference to make in india order dtd or later the make in india order shall also be treated as breach of code of integrity
the fact and duration of debarment for this reason by any procuring entity must be promptly brought to the notice of the of the standing committee under the make in india order and the department of expenditure through the concerned ministry or in some other manner
on periodical basis such cases shall be consolidated and centralized list or decentralized lists of such suppliers with the period of debarment must be maintained and displayed on website
supplier who has been debarred by any procuring entity as this sub para shall not be eligible for preference under the make in india order for procurement by any other procuring entity for the duration of the debarment
this shall be effective from the date of uploading of such debarment on the website
iii for any actions or omissions by the bidder other than violation of code of integrity which in the opinion of the warrants debarment for the reasons like supply of material of material abandonment of works quality of works failure to abide by bid securing declaration etc
effective date for the procuring entities which has carried out the debarment he period of debarment starts from the date of issue of debarment order
in respect of procuring entities other than the one which has carried out the debarment the debarment takes effect prospectively from the date of uploading on the website in such manner that ongoing procurements are not disrupted
jurisdiction it shall not be circulated to other departments
it will only be applicable to all the subordinate offices autonomous bodies central public sector undertakings cpses etc
of the department issuing the debarment order
process of debarment the concerned department before issuing the debarment order against firm must ensure that reasonable opportunity has been given to the concerned firm to represent against such debarment including personal hearing if requested by firm
secretary of may nominate an officer at the rank of joint secretary as competent authority ca to debar the firms
iii the will maintain list of debarred firms mentioning the jurisdiction and period of debarment which will also be displayed on its website
iv debarment is an executive function and should not be allocated to vigilance timeline of debarment process the period of debarment starts from the date of issue of debarment order therefore the process of debarment should be conducted in an expeditious manner
considering the nature of such proceedings and need to afford fair hearing to the firm following timeline is suggested which may be suitably modified considering the specifics of an organisation noticing of delinquency of the firm by the procuring entity zero day evaluation of evidence and proposal to ca for banning of the firm weeks iii issue of show cause notice to the firm calling for written and oral submission
iv time for submission including reminders etc weeks
evaluation of firm submission and giving oral hearing to firm weeks vi final order indicating opportunity to the firm weeks time to appeal to the secretary of department as appellate authority weeks
vii total weeks from zero day after which debarment period starts
viii receipt of appeal and disposal the same by the appellate authority weeks
debarment by cpses attached autonomous bodies gem it is possible that the firm may be debarred concurrently by more than one department
departments at their option may also delegate powers to debar bidders to their cpses attached autonomous bodies etc
in such cases broad principles for debarment in to vii above are to be kept in mind
debarment by such bodies like cpses etc
shall be applicable only for the procurements made by such bodies
similarly government gem can also debar bidders up to two years on its portal
debarment across all departments where department is of the view that business dealings with particular firm should be banned across all the departments by debarring the firm from taking part in any tendering procedure floated by the central government departments the department concerned should after obtaining the approval of the secretary concerned forward to doe note setting out all the facts of the case and the justification for the proposed debarment along with all the relevant papers and documents
doe will issue the necessary orders after satisfying itself that proposed debarment across all the departments is in accordance with rule of gfrs
this scrutiny is intended to ensure uniformity of treatment in all cases
department before forwarding the proposal to doe must ensure that reasonable opportunity has been given to the concerned firm to represent against such debarment including personal hearing if requested by firm
if doe realizes that sufficient opportunity has not be given to the firm to represent against the debarment such debarment requests received from departments shall be rejected
the firm shall remain debarred during the interim period till the final decision taken by doe only in the department forwarding such proposal
for this purpose the proposing ministry shall issue an order debarring the firm from taking part in tendering procedures floated by their department following the procedure laid down in above
such order must mention that the government reserves its right to debar the firm from taking part in any tendering procedure floated across all the central government departments following due procedure
doe can also give additional opportunity at their option to firm to represent against proposed debarment
doe can also take action to debar the firms in certain circumstances
doe will maintain list of such debarred firms mentioning the jurisdiction and period of debarment which will be displayed on central public procurement portal
doe shall complete the process of debarment within weeks after receiving proposal from the concerned department
no contract of any kind whatsoever shall be placed on the firm debarred by doe including its allied firms by any offices of the government of india including autonomous body cpses etc
after the issue of debarment order
review and revocation of orders an order for debarment passed shall be deemed to have been automatically revoked on the expiry of period of debarment specified therein and it will not be necessary to issue specific formal order of revocation
the authorised entity doe department or cpses attached autonomous bodies gem etc that issued the order of debarment can review or revoke the debarment order before the period of debarment is over based on new facts that come to light or on an appeal by the debarred bidder
after review an order for modification of period of debarment or for revocation of debarment if there is adequate justification for the same can be issued
ordinarily such revocation of the order should be done with the approval of secretary concerned of doe or the which issued such orders
in case of debarments done by cpses attached autonomous bodies gem etc such revocation of the debarment orders should be done only with the approval of chief executive officer
other provisions common to both types of debarments no contract of any kind whatsoever shall be placed to debarred firm including its allied firms after the issue of debarment order by the department
bids from only such firms shall be considered for placement of contract which are neither debarred on the date of opening of tender opening of first bid normally called as technical bid in case of two stage tendering nor debarred on the date of contract date of issue of letter of acceptance
even in the cases of risk purchase no contract should be placed on such debarred firms
if case any debarred firms has submitted the bid the same will be ignored
in case such firm is lowest next lowest firm shall be considered as
bid security submitted by such debarred firms shall be returned to them
contracts concluded before the issue of the debarment order shall not be affected by the debarment orders
the debarment shall be automatically extended to all its allied firms
in case of joint consortium is debarred all partners will also stand debarred for the period specified in debarment order
the names of partners should be clearly specified in the debarment debarment in any manner does not impact any other contractual or other legal rights of the procuring entities
the period of debarment shall start from the date of issue of debarment order
the order of debarment will indicate the reason in brief that led to debarment of the firm
ordinarily the period of debarment should not be less than six months
in case of shortage of suppliers in particular group such debarments may also hurt the interest of procuring entities
in such cases endeavour should be to pragmatically analyse the circumstances try to reform the supplier and may get written commitment from the supplier that its performance will improve
all departments must align their existing debarment guidelines in conformity with these guidelines
further tender documents must also be suitably amended if required
safeguarding procuring entity interests during debarment of suppliers suppliers are important assets for the procuring entities and punishing delinquent suppliers should be the last resort
it takes lot of time and effort to develop register and mature new supplier
in case of shortage of suppliers in particular group of such punishment may also hurt the interest of procuring entity
therefore views of the concerned department may always be sought about the repercussions of such punitive action on the continuity of procurements
past records of performance of the supplier may also be given due weightage
in case of shortage of suppliers and in cases of less serious misdemeanours the endeavour should be to pragmatically analyse the circumstances reform the supplier and get written commitment from the supplier that his performance will improve
if this fails efforts should be to see if temporary debarment can serve the purpose

grievances and its redressal any supplier contractor or consultant that claims to have suffered or is likely to suffer loss or injury due to breach of fundamental principles of procurement by the procuring entity may make an application for review of such decision action or omission within period of five days from the date of such decision or action to the designated officer named in the tender documents in this regard or the head of the procuring entity if not so specified specifying the ground and the relevant clauses of the tender documents
this grievance redressal mechanism is apart from the vigilance channel of complaints
unsuccessful bidders may seek regarding the rejection of his bid in writing or electronically within days of declaration of or financial evaluation results
only directly affected bidder can represent in this regard only bidder who has participated in the concerned procurement process qualification bidder registration or bidding as the case may be can make such representation
in case bid has been evaluated before the bidding of financial bids an application for review in relation to the financial bid may be filed only by bidder has qualified in bid in case technical bid has been evaluated before the opening of the financial bid an application for review in relation to the financial bid may be filed only by bidder whose technical bid is found to be acceptable
following decisions of the procuring entity in accordance with the provision of internal guidelines shall not be subject to review determination of the need for procurement selection of the mode of procurement or tendering system iii choice of selection procedure iv complaints against activity schedule except under the premise that they are either vague or too specific to limit competition may be permissible
provisions limiting participation of bidders in the procurement process in terms of policies of the government
vi provisions regarding purchase preferences to specific categories of bidders in terms of policies of the government vii the decision to enter into negotiations with the bidder viii cancellation of the procurement process except where it is intended to subsequently the same requirements ix issues related to ambiguity in contract terms may not be taken up after contract has been signed all such issues should be highlighted before consummation of the contract by the
within five working days of receipt of the complaint the designated officer shall acknowledge the receipt in writing to the complainant indicating that it has been received and the response shall be sent in due course after detailed examination
the redressal of the grievance must be completed within thirty days of its receipt
the designated officer would call comments of concerned procurement officers and take view about further processing of the grievance and may also decide whether the process of procurement should be put on hold for the or not
if the designated officer on receipt of comments of relevant officer finds complaint to have substance appropriate and feasible remedial measure should be initiated
if the grievance is resolved or if the grievance is found to be unwarranted the final decision shall be informed to the aggrieved party in writing after approval by the competent authority of the procurement
if the grievance is not redressed within days or if the bidder or prospective bidder is aggrieved by the decision of the designated officer the bidder or prospective bidder may file an application for redressal to the appellate authority mentioned in the tender documents head of procuring organisation if not so specified within period of fifteen days thereafter
investigations of serious deviations from procurement guidelines or based on representations from bidders the designated officer or appellate authority may if considers that an investigation is necessary or desirable for the purpose of preventing investigating or detecting serious deviations from procurement guidelines appoint person or persons at sufficiently higher level than the officers involved to investigate any matter related to the conduct of any procurement proceedings or the conclusion or operation of any procurement contract
the appointed investigator shall carry out the investigation and report the compliance to the procurement guidelines to the appellate authority
if the designated officer or appellate authority is satisfied that there has been contravention of procurement guidelines in relation to any procurement proceedings or procurement contract he may initiate such action as in his opinion is necessary to rectify the contravention including handing over the case for further investigation to cvo or through cvo to cbi if there are aspect which require police investigations
registration of fir and instituting legal proceedings for prosecution in appropriate court of law
annulment of the procurement proceedings cancellation of the procurement contract if legally feasible in case any individual staff is found responsible suitable disciplinary proceedings should be initiated against such staff under the conduct rules
in case of complicity of any bidder is proved removal of concerned firm from list of registered firms debarment of the bidders if warranted iii reporting the matter to competition commission of india cci in case of competitive actions by the bidder
if the grievance is due to inadequacy of procurement guidelines or due to lack of understanding of the staff remedial action to address such lacunae may be initiated without repercussion to the concerned staff
hospitality hospitality including facilitation of travel lodging boarding and entertainment during official or unofficial programs from service providers may tend to cross the limits of normal business practice
officials sent to firm premises for meetings may mistakenly presume entitlement to hospitality from the firm even if other arrangements are available at the location
hospitality must never be solicited directly or indirectly
the frequency scale and number of officials availing hospitality should not be allowed to identify the recipient in public way with any particular service provider or raise doubts about its neutrality
it should not involve significant travel overnight accommodation or trips abroad
particular care should be taken in relation to offers of hospitality from firms say participating in current or imminent tenders or its execution who stand to derive personal or commercial benefit from their relationship with the recipient
gifts gifts from service providers may tend to cross the limits of normal business practice especially on festive season
since the value of the gift may not be known to the recipient it may cause inadvertent violation of conduct rules
gifts must never be solicited directly or indirectly
an official should not accept and retain gifts more valuable than the limit as laid down in the conduct rules
particular care should be taken in relation to gifts from firms say participating in current or imminent tenders or its execution who stand to derive personal or commercial benefit from their relationship with the recipient
cash gift cheques or any vouchers that may be exchanged for cash may not be accepted regardless of the amount
any gift received inadvertently in violation of above must immediately either be returned or else reported and deposited in treasury
private purchases from official service providers procuring officials may mistakenly consider it innocuous to seek discounts in private procurements from service providers having official dealings or its associates especially against rate contracts
public purchasers must not seek or accept special facilities or discounts on private purchases particularly same items which are being ordered officially from contractors service providers including rate contract holders with whom they have official dealings
sponsorship of events procuring officials may mistakenly consider it innocuous to seek financial public purchasers must never get involved in any pecuniary transaction with the contractors
conduct of public servants in public procurement risks and mitigations favours donations advertisements for souvenirs and contributions in cash or kind in relation to sponsoring of cultural social charitable religious or sporting events in the false belief that since she is personally not benefitted it would not be violation of cipp
service providers including soliciting of sponsorship for unofficial and private cultural social sporting religious charitable or similar organisations or events from
conflict of interest coi para above code of integrity for public procurement has provision on conflict of interest which states if the bidding firm or their personnel have relationships or financial or business transactions with any official of procuring entity who are directly or indirectly related to tender or execution process of contract there may be dilemma regarding the officers related to the tender or execution process and if even minor routine transactions
officers related to the tender or execution process would depend on the organisational structure and sensitivity of their role in procurement
it may cover key officials and any external advisors involved in making recommendation various approvals or making an important decision at any stage in procurement during need indenting tender document preparation of comparative tabulation technical and financial evaluation of bids signing of contract execution of contract payments to the contractor
coi can be in the nature of significant business interests family relationship regular social interactions close personal friendships
conflict of interest actual potential or perceived can arise when any senior executive or team handling the bidding at the firm bidding for the contract called firm team has such transaction with officials or their close relatives mentioned in sub above
examples such official or his close family relative their family their family has substantial business interests in the firm say shares more than of market cap taken financial obligation availed hospitality say beyond the limits laid down in code of conduct of the organisation have previously worked for the firm or are close personal friend of the firm team members or regularly say more than once in quarter interact socially clubs games social associations with them

types of contracts there is different basis for linking payments to the performance of services called types of contracts each having different risks and mitigation measures
bids are called and evaluated based on the type of contract
the choice of the type of contract should be based on vfm with due regard to the nature of assignment
adoption of an inappropriate type of contract could lead to situation of lack of competition contractual disputes and of the contract
each type of contract is described briefly in subsequent paras and criteria are suggested for their adoption along with risks and mitigation measures
mostly used types of contracts are lump sum firm fixed price contract time based contracts percentage success fee contract cum success contract indefinite delivery contract
lump sum firm fixed price contract the lump sum firm fixed price contract is the simplest form of contract and wherever feasible the procuring entity shall use this form of contract
consultant proposal is deemed to include all prices no arithmetical correction or price adjustments are allowed during evaluation
lump sum consultancy contracts are easy to administer because there is fixed price for fixed scope and payments are linked to clearly specified deliverables such as reports documents drawings bills of quantities software programs and so on
bidders quote lump sum price for the required quantum of services
they may also be asked to quote unit rate for the consultancy output to be used in case of variation schedule of requirement shall indicate the quantum of the consultancy outputs its performance standards and the milestones of its delivery
contract may specify parts of payments to be released at specified milestones
in view of risks mentioned below this type of contracts are widely used for simple planning and feasibility studies environmental studies detailed design of standard or common structures preparation of data processing systems and so forth
lump sum contracts risks and mitigations service provider to cut corners on quality and scope of the deliverables by saving on resources employed
disputes may arise due to different possible interpretations of quality and scope of assignment
of the service providers are clearly defined
the contract should include provision for evaluation of quality and scope of deliverables and certificate for its acceptability may be recorded
payment should be made only against certificate of acceptance of deliverables
time as time is not linked to the payment
there may be tendency for the service provider to save on deployment of resources which may result in
while the payments are not linked to time the assignment should be monitored per month to ensure that the output per month is in line with planned and estimated
deliverables as in contracts is not linked to the payment
there may be tendency for the service provider to cut corners on quality scope and timing of the deliverables by saving on resources employed
disputes may arise quality and scope of assignment
payments should be released only against such certificates
performance in each time period is not linked to the payment
there may be tendency for the service provider contracts need to be closely monitored and administered by the entity to ensure that the progress of assignment is commensurate with the time spent and that
contract in contracts payments are based on agreed hourly daily weekly or monthly rates for staff who in consultancy contracts are normally named and on reimbursable items using actual expenses agreed unit prices
these are also called as retainer ship contracts since the service provider are retained for decided contract period
the rates for staff include salary social costs overhead fee or profit and where appropriate special allowances
schedule of requirement shall indicate the quantum of inputs required of different key and personnel qualifications of reimbursable items and the milestones of its deliverables
this type of contract is appropriate when lump sum contract is not feasible due to difficulties in defining the scope and the length of services either because the inputs required for attaining the objectives of the assignment is difficult to assess or because the services are tied up to activities by others for which the completion period may vary
because of risks and mitigations mentioned below this type of contract is widely used for complex studies supervision of construction advisory services and most training assignments etc
contracts risks and mitigations to use paid staff in dilatory and productive manner
the resources for which payment is claimed have actually efficiently and productively been deployed on the assignment during the period
system of monthly reporting of payouts and quantum of work achieved by the service provider to ca should be instituted to enable supervision
time and cost is major risk in contracts as the payment is based on time and delay may result in unanticipated benefit to the consultant and the assignment may get delayed
this type of contract should include an upper limit of total payments to be made to the service providers for the assignment to safeguard against excessive prolonging of time and payments
after this limit is reached or the period of completion is exceeded ca should review justification for extension of the contract

percentage contingency fee contract percentage contingency fee contracts directly relate the fees paid to the service provider to the estimated or actual project cost or the cost of the goods procured or inspected
since the payment is made after the successful realisation of objectives it is also called success or contingency fee contract
the final selection is made among the technically qualified consultants who have quoted the lowest percentage while the notional value of assets is fixed
schedule of requirement shall indicate the estimated value of transactions to be handled as well as the contract period one year unless otherwise stipulated over which such volume shall be availed
however there shall be no firm commitment to avail the entire value of transactions within the contract period
due to risks and mitigations discussed below these contracts are commonly used for appropriate architectural services procurement and inspection agents
percentage contracts risks and mitigations cost of the project in the case of architectural or engineering services percentage contracts implicitly lack incentive for economic design and are hence discouraged
if it is based on fixed target cost and covers precisely defined services
all risks as applicable to both percentage contracts and contracts are encountered in this case same mitigation strategies as in both percentage and contracts may be adopted in this case
retainer and success contingency fee contract in retainer and success contingency fee contracts the remuneration of the consultant includes retainer time based monthly payment and success fee percentage based the latter being normally expressed as percentage of the estimated or actual project cost
thus this type of contract is combination of time based and percentage contracts
due to risks and mitigations discussed below retainer and contingency fee contracts are widely used when consultants banks or financial firms are preparing companies for sales or mergers of firms notably in privatization operations
it can also be used for assignments related to organisational change
and contingency fee contracts risks and mitigations
indefinite delivery contract price agreement these contracts are used when procuring entity need to have on call specialized services the extent and timing of which can not be defined in advance
this is akin to the system of contracts or framework contracts in the procurement of goods
there is no commitment from procuring entity for the quantum of work that may be assigned to the consultant
the procuring entity and the firm agree on the unit rates to be paid and payments are made on the basis of the quantum of service actually used
the service provider shall be selected based on the unit rate quoted by them for providing the services
schedule of requirement shall indicate only tentative estimate of the volume of required service as well as the contract period one year unless otherwise stipulated over which such volume is likely to be availed
the services shall be availed as and when needed by the procuring entity without any commitment regarding the volume of services
due to risks and mitigations discussed below indefinite delivery contracts are commonly used to retain advisers or avail services for example expert adjudicators for dispute resolution panels institutional reforms procurement advice technical troubleshooting document management taxi services temporary manpower deployment and so forth normally over period of year or more
risk of indefinite delivery contracts are at risk of being in excess of actual need since the scrutiny of service need may not be as intense as in case of other types of contracts
the need assessment of utilized services should be subject to some scrutiny to ensure that there is no abnormal unexplainable trend in utilization
such contracts need to be closely monitored and administered by the entity to ensure that the there is no indiscriminate or unwarranted usage and maximum contract value may be laid down to keep control over usage and approval of ca may be obtained to extend it beyond such limit
in the report monthly payout benchmark may be kept above which the report may be required to be sent to level above ca
the quality and scope of the deliverables as in contracts is not linked to the payment
there may be tendency for the service provider to use resources in dilatory and manner
contracts need to be closely monitored and progress of assignment is commensurate with the time spent and that the resources for which payment is claimed have actually efficiently and productively been deployed on the assignment during the period
system of monthly reporting of payouts and quantum of work achieved by the service provider to ca time and cost is major risk in such contracts as the output may not be achieved in the estimated time
this type of contract should include an upper limit of total payments to be made to the service providers to safeguard against excessive prolonging of time and payments
indefinite delivery contracts risks and mitigations
systems of selection of service providers since the quality and scope of consultancy assignment are not tangibly identifiable and consistently measurable the technical and financial capability of consultants becomes an important though indirect determinant for quality and scope of performance
in such situation value for money is achieved by encouraging wide and open competition among equally competent consultant
thus selection of consultants is normally done in process
in the first stage likely capable sources are shortlisted on the basis of qualification and experience requirements for the given assignment for further consideration if need be through an of interest eoi through advertisement
the shortlist should include sufficient number not fewer than three and not more than eight eligible firms
in rare cases where less than three consultants become eligible as per criteria and the criteria can not be relaxed procurement may be continued with the approval of the competent authority
in the second stage the shortlisted consultants are invited to submit their technical and financial rfp proposals generally in separate sealed envelopes
evaluation of the technical proposal is carried out by evaluators without access to the financial part of the proposal
financial proposals are opened after evaluation of quality
the relative importance of quality and price aspects may vary from assignment to assignment depending on criticality of quality requirements internal capability of procuring entity to engage and supervise the assignment as well as the value of procurements
hence different systems of selection of service providers are designed to achieve appropriate relative importance weightage of quality and price aspects
decision on system of selection is normally preceded by an assessment of the capacity of the user to engage and supervise the implementation of proposed assignment
the selection method chosen depends to some extent on this assessment
selection of system of selection also should consider the likely field of bidders
the nomenclature of various selection methods below is in line with generally prevalent nomenclature price based system least cost selection lcs quality and cost based selection qcbs direct selection single source selection sss fixed budget based selection fbs
price based system least cost selection lcs in this method of selection service providers submit both technical proposal and financial proposal at the same time
minimum qualifying marks for quality of the technical proposal are prescribed as benchmark normally out of maximum hundred and indicated in the rfp along with scheme for allotting marks for various technical attributes
alternatively since in lcs selection technical offers do not require be ranked or to be added of weighted technical score to financial score as in qcbs selection it would suffice in appropriately simple cases similar to eoi criteria please refer to para if the evaluation criteria is only pass criteria prescribing only the minimum qualifying benchmark
thus in lcs simplified evaluation criteria may also be used where instead of marking scheme minimum benchmark of technical evaluation may be prescribed
must have completed at least two similar assignments must have turnover of at least rs rupees ten crore etc
any bidder that passes these benchmarks is declared as technically qualified for opening of their technical criteria may not be relevant to realization of quality of assignment
technical criteria selected should be relevant and proportional to the requirement of quality of assignment and the selection process should be rigorous enough to ensure that on one hand no technically unsatisfactory bids should be able to get past loose criteria and on the other hand no technically satisfactory offer should get ruled out by tight criteria
marking subjectivity the scheme of marking or its application may be subjective
it is important to lay down as objective scheme of marking as possible
cases where subjectivity is unavoidable as in evaluation of methodology etc system of grading responses and their marking may be laid down in the bidding documents
procuring entity should also have system of conciliation and moderation of widely disparate markings by different members of evaluation committee
the technical proposals are opened first and evaluated and the offers who are qualifying as per these technical evaluation criteria will only be considered as technically responsive and the rest would be considered technically nonresponsive and would be dropped from the list
financial proposals are then opened for only eligible and responsive offers financial bids of other unresponsive bidders are returned unopened and ranked
offer out of the responsive offers is selected on price criteria alone without giving any additional weightage to ranking of technical proposal
this system of selection is roughly the same as the selection of offer among the technically responsive offers in procurement of works
rule of gfr also see para lcs is considered suitable for recruiting service providers from firms in most assignments that are of standard or routine nature such as engineering design of works where practices and standards exist
it is the simplest and the quickest system of selection and under normal circumstances this method of evaluation shall be used as default since it allows for minimum satisfactory technical efficiency with economy
justification must be provided if selection method other than lcs is to be used
least cost selection risks and mitigations
quality and cost based selection qcbs in qcbs system of selection both the quality of the proposal and the cost of the services are considered as deciding factors
this approach is employed when the quality of deliverables is crucial but the cost of service or work can not be ignored
technical scores are assigned to proposals based on specified quality criteria
minimum qualifying marks normally seventy eighty out of maximum hundred marks as benchmark for quality of the technical proposal is prescribed and description remarks score weighting high assignments use qcbs with higher technical weightage moderate complexity majority of cases will follow this range assignments of standard or routine nature such as agents handling the procurement use of lcs is appropriate inappropriate selection of qcbs there is possibility that qcbs system is selected where lcs or other systems would have been more appropriate considering the quality requirements or the capability of procuring entity to monitor the assignment
selection of qcbs should be justified and applied only under circumstances mentioned above
weightage of technical cost may not be proportional to quality requirements weightage different from seventy thirty should be adequately examined and justified
proposals below this benchmark are not considered for financial evaluation
the financial proposals are also given based on relative ranking of prices with hundred marks for the lowest and lower marks for higher priced offers
the total score shall be obtained by weighting the quality and cost scores and adding them
for example the weightage given to cost score may be thirty percent and technical score may be given weightage of seventy percent but should never be more than
the ratio of weightages for cost and technical score could also be forty sixty or fifty fifty etc
however the weight for the cost shall be chosen considering the complexity of the assignment and the relative importance of quality
the proposed weightings for quality and cost shall be specified in the rfp
the firm obtaining the highest total score shall be selected
it may be noted that theoretically qcbs system with weight of hundred percent for the cost approximates the price based lcs system
this method of selection shall be used for highly technically complex and critical assignments where it is justifiable to pay appropriately higher price for higher quality of proposal
table below provides suggestive weighting for qcbs
rule of gfr also see para table

direct selection single source selection sss under some special circumstances it may become necessary to select particular service provider where adequate justification is available for such selection in the context of the overall interest of procuring entity
in finance ministry of policies and procedure of employment of consultants this is called dns which is not the generally prevalent nomenclature
rule of gfr also see para the selection by nomination is permissible under exceptional circumstance such as tasks that represent natural continuation of previous work carried out by the firm in case of an emergency situation situations arising after natural disasters situations where timely completion of the assignment is of utmost importance situations where execution of the assignment may involve use of proprietary techniques or only one consultant has requisite expertise at times other psus or government organizations are used to provide technical expertise
it is possible to use the expertise of such institutions on sss basis under some special circumstances it may become necessary to select particular consultant where adequate justification is available for such selection in the context of the overall interest of the ministry or department
full justification for single source selection should be recorded in the file and approval of the competent authority obtained before resorting to such selection
procuring entity shall ensure fairness and equity and shall have procedure in place to ensure that the prices are reasonable and consistent with market rates for tasks of similar nature and the required consultancy services are not split into smaller sized procurement
all consultancy contracts awarded on nomination basis should be brought to the notice of following authorities for the secretary in case of
the board of directors or equivalent managing body in case of public sector undertakings public sector banks insurance companies etc inappropriate selection of sss there is possibility that sss system is selected where lcs or other systems would have been more appropriate considering the quality requirements or the capability of procuring entity to monitor the assignment
the assignment may be split into parcels to avoid competitive selection systems or to avoid obtaining higher level approvals for sss
full justification for single source selection should be recorded in the file and approval of the competent authority schedule of procurement powers sopp should severely restrict powers for sss selection obtained before resorting to such source selection
in direct selection the procuring entity should ensure fairness and equity and the required consultancy services are not split into smaller sized procurement to avoid competitive processes
cost may be unreasonably high the single service provider is likely to charge unreasonably high price
procuring entity must have procedure in place to ensure that the prices are reasonable and consistent with market rates for tasks of similar nature
if necessary negotiations may be held with the service providers to examine reasonableness of quoted price
the chief executive of the organisation where such managing body is not in existence
the report relating to such awards on nomination basis shall be submitted to the executive managing body every quarter
the audit committee or similar unit in the organisation may be required to check at least of such cases
sss risks and mitigations
fixed budget based selection fbs for consultancy services gfrs provide three methods for of consultancy proposals viz
quality and cost based selection qcbs least cost system lcs and single source selection sss
the fixed budget based selection fbs method is now also for selection of consultants
in fbs the selection process considers both the quality of proposals and the cost
fbs is competitive method encouraging consultants to provide services within the defined budget constraints
fixed budget in the request for proposal rfp document specific fixed budget is specified
consultants must adhere to this budget and their proposed cost can not exceed it
quality assessment consultants submit their proposals and the evaluation considers the quality of these proposals
the proposal that scores the highest in quality and is within the specified budget is selected for award of contract
this general instructions on procurement and project management doe om dtd october assessment ensures that the selected consultant meets the project requirements effectively within the stipulated budget
fbs may be used when the type of consulting services required is simple repetitive and can be precisely defined and the budget can be reasonable estimated and set based on credible cost estimates or previous selections which have been successfully executed and the budget is sufficient for the consultant to perform the assignment
modes of procurement offers from prospective bidders in public procurement must be invited according to procedure that achieves balance between the need for the widest competition on one hand and complexity of the procedure on the other hand
different modes of procurement and tendering systems are used to suit various procurement circumstances to achieve this balance
there are laid down procedures for delegation of powers of procurement to various competent authorities under different modes as shown in dfpr
each procuring entity may also publish its own schedule of procurement powers sopp delegating such powers within the entity
suggested format for sopp is given at annexure
however as mentioned in para applicability of this manual for procurements financed by extended by international agencies like the world bank asian development bank the procurement procedures as finalized and incorporated in the articles of agreements with such agencies for relevant grants after consideration and approval of the ministry of finance are to be followed
the various modes of procurement that can be used in public procurement are open tenders open tender enquiry ote and global tender enquiry gte iii rate contracts procurement through selected suppliers limited tender enquiry lte up to rs
rupees lakh and special limited tender enquiry slte above rs
rupees lakhs under exceptional circumstances nomination basis tenders single tender enquiry ste without pac procurements without calling tenders direct procurement without quotation direct procurement by purchase committee dynamic price discovery electronic reverse auction era applicability terms and conditions risks and mitigations of these modes of procurements including restrictions regarding gte mode for procurements below rs crore are detailed in chapter of the manual for procurement of goods which may be referred
for sake of brevity these are not repeated here
rule of gfr manual for procurement of consultancy services
bidding systems bidding systems are designed to achieve an appropriate balance between the countervailing needs for right quality right source and the right price under different criticality of technical requirements and value of procurements
in certain critical and complex requirements the technical and financial capability of source of supply becomes an important determinant for value for money
depending on the complexity and criticality technical of requirement criticality of capability of source and value of procurement following types of tendering systems may be used
the various bidding systems that are used in public procurement are single stage tendering system single stage single envelop system single stage two envelops system two bid system rule of gfr iii single stage multiple envelops system with
two stage bidding expression of interest tenders market listing rule of gfr
details of these bidding systems are explained in chapter of the manual for procurement of goods which may be referred
channels of procurement public procurement can be channelled by way of manual bids eprocurement platforms gem portal or through agencies
electronic procurement rule of gfr electronic procurement is the use of information and communication technology specially the internet by the buyer through third party portal in conducting procurement processes with the contractors for the acquisition of goods supplies works and services aimed at open and efficient procurement through transparent procedures
generic description of how is conducted is given in appendix of the goods manual
it is mandatory for all of the central government their attached and subordinate offices and bodies to publish their tender enquiries corrigenda thereof and details of bid awards online on the central public procurement portal cppp and also on their website
these instructions apply to all tender enquiries requests for proposals requests for expressions of interest notice for registration or any other notice inviting bids or proposals in any form whether they are advertised issued to limited number of parties or to single party
these instructions would not apply to purchase of goods without quotations or purchase of goods by purchase committee upto rs lakhs
normally in no manual tender documents are provided nor any manual bids are accepted
it is not good practice to call both electronic as well as manual bids in the same tender
and below allow exemptions in specific situations mentioned therein from in cases where it is not convenient or feasible
in global tender enquiry by any mode open tender limited tender or single tender may not be mandatorily insisted upon however would still be mandatory
in individual cases where national security and strategic considerations demands confidentiality departments may exempt such cases from procurement after seeking approval of concerned secretary the head of the body in the case of autonomous and statutory bodies with the concurrence of financial advisers
in case of tenders floated by indian missions abroad competent authority to decide the tender may exempt such case from
should be obtained in each such case
statistical information on the number of cases in which exemption was granted and the value of the concerned contract should be intimated on quarterly basis to the ministry of finance department of expenditure
items costing less than rs lakh can be purchased provided such items are not available on gem through direct procurement without quotation or through purchase committee but refer para would still be mandatory for all procurements without lower value limit
national informatics centre nic has an portal called government procurement of nic gepnic
there are other service providers in public sector mstc and private sector which can be utilized for
details about the process of are available from the service providers
appendix of the goods manual also gives such generic details of the process
departments which do not have large volume of procurement or carry out procurements required only for running of offices and have not initiated procurement through any other solution provided so far may use solution developed by nic
other departments may either use solution developed by nic or engage any other service provider following due process
these instructions will not apply to procurements made by departments through government gem
mandatory procurement of goods and services through government marketplace gem government electronic marketplace is type of site where product or services are offered by several sellers and all the buyers can select the services offered by any one of the sellers based on his own criteria
in an online marketplace purchaser transactions are processed by the marketplace operator and then services are delivered and fulfilled directly by the participating retailers
other capabilities included are auctioning forward or reverse catalogues ordering posting of requirements by purchasers payment gateways etc
the procurement process on gem is ended to end from placement of supply order to payment to suppliers
this is to ensure better transparency and higher efficiency
the procurement of goods and services by ministries or departments is mandatory for goods or services available on gem as per rule of gfr
guidelines for gem are detailed in chapter of the manual for procurement of goods which may be referred
procurement through centralized agencies or other organizations organisations who have not their own infrastructure for purchase may engage procurement agents for individual procurement or as outsourcing of service with the approval of its secretary
many canalized agencies authorised by the government and some do provide such procurement services framing procurement documents bidding process evaluation and contract management
procurements by such agencies would have to conform to these procurement guidelines
in such cases contract can be placed on them for procurement services at mutually agreed terms
guidelines for procurement through such agencies are detailed in chapter of the manual for procurement of goods which may be referred
examples not an exhaustive or recommendatory list of such agencies are rail india technical and economic services rites delhi metro rail corporation dmrc engineers india limited eil indian railway institute of logistics and materials management irilmm institute of public auditors of india ipai etc
model tender documents department of expenditure doe ministry of finance government of india has issued model tender documents for procurement of procurement of consultancy and procurement of on october
procuring entities are urged to customise relevant mtd for preparing tender documents for their procurements
guidance notes annexed to the mtds detail the process of customisation of mtd for an organisation and for each procurement
the tender document is the fundamental document in the public procurement process as after award of the contract it becomes part of the contract agreement
carefully prepared tender document avoids delays and complaints
this will also attract more bidders to formulate and submit their competitive bids with confidence
hence it is worth spending time and effort on this even in cases of urgency
clauses in the tender document should be clear and comprehensive without any ambiguity
to avoid differences in interpretation and possible disputes time overrun cost overrun and quality compromises
while tender document should be complete in themselves and may be slightly different for various categories of procurements these must necessarily address the essential aspects mentioned below rule of gfr
model tender documents issued by the doe which comply with all these requirements may be used with due customisation as per the guidance notes annexed to the mtds description of the subject matter of procurement its drawings including the quality assurance quantity time and place or places of completion limitation or preference for participation by bidders in terms of the government policies the procedure as well as date time and place for obtaining submitting and opening of the bids from ds accessible from df from notified under para vide om issued by department of expenditure dated suitable provisions for enabling bidder to question the bidding conditions bidding process rejection of its bid
these provisions should include time frame in which procuring entity will address the bidder questions criteria for determining the responsiveness of bids criteria as well as factors to be considered for evaluating the bids on common platform and the criteria for awarding the contract to the responsive most advantageous as the case may be bidder should be clearly indicated in the tender documents the eligibility criteria should take care of the supplier eligibility to participate in the tender process
the qualification criteria for the bidders should take care of its capability to perform the resultant contract successfully balancing considerations of quality time and cost
commercial terms and conditions payment terms tax implications respective obligations of the procuring entity and the suppliers compliance framework for statutory and other norms
provision of price variation wherever considered appropriate as well as methodology for calculation of the same shall be clearly stipulated in the tender document
tender document should include clause that if firm quotes nil the bid shall be treated as unresponsive and will not be procedures for redressal of grievances or complaints from aggrieved bidders if applicable integrity pact clause and format to be signed shall be included suitable provision for settlement of disputes if any emanating from the resultant contract should be kept in the tender document and essential terms of the procurement contract including suitable clause mentioning that the resultant contract will be interpreted under indian laws
procuring entities may issue instructions regarding appropriate delegation of authority for approval of the tender documents before these are uploaded
eligibility criteria specifies the very basic criteria that abider should meet to be considered responsive bid to be evaluated further beyond the preliminary screening of bids
qualification criteria technical and financial qualification criteria for the bidders are important in the public procurement process
they shall be clear and fair having regard to the specific circumstances of the procurement
appropriate parameters should be prescribed in the qualification criteria for bidders to enable selection of the right type of bidders in public interest balancing considerations of quality time and cost
evaluation criteria procuring entity may include in the evaluation criteria in the tender document based on one or more of quality price technical merit aesthetic and functional characteristics environmental characteristics running costs effectiveness sales service and technical assistance delivery date and delivery period or period of completion etc
no criteria shall be used for evaluation of tenders that can not be verified or has not been specified in the tender document
open online tendering should be the default method to ensure efficiency of procurement
public authorities should also keep the experience criteria broad based so that bidders with experience in similar nature of goods can participate
the procuring entity should allow enough time to the bidders to prepare their proposals
the time allowed shall depend on the assignment but normally shall not be less than four weeks and not more than three months
in cases where participation of international consultants is contemplated period of not less than eight weeks should normally be allowed
